<p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;params=47_0_N_28_55_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">47°0′N</span> <span class="longitude">28°55′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">47.000°N 28.917°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">47.000; 28.917</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></p>
<p><b>Chișinău</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/ 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/aʊ/ 'ou' in 'pout'">aʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Romanian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Romanian" title="Help:IPA for Romanian">[kiʃiˈnəw]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">Кишинёв, <i>Kishinëv</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk" xml:lang="uk">Кишинів</span>), also known formerly as <b>Kishinev</b> and Kichineff, is the capital and largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Republic of Moldova</a>. The city is Moldova's main industrial and commercial center, and is located in the middle of the country, on the river <a href="/wiki/B%C3%AEc_River" title="Bîc River">Bîc</a>. According to the preliminary results of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Census_(2014)" title="Moldovan Census (2014)">2014 census</a>, the city of Chișinău is home to 492,894 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-PopCensus2014_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopCensus2014-3">[3]</a></sup> The estimated number of resident population in the Municipality of Chișinău (which includes other nearby communities), as of 1 January 2015, is 736,100.<sup id="cite_ref-Estimates_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estimates-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chișinău is the most economically prosperous locality in Moldova and its largest transportation hub.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_names">Etymology and names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The origin of the city's name is unclear.</p>
<p>In one version, the name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Archaism" title="Archaism">archaic</a> Romanian word <i>chișla</i> (meaning "spring", "source of water") and <i>nouă</i> ("new"), because it was built around a small spring, at the corner of Pușkin and Albișoara streets.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The other version, formulated by <a href="/wiki/%C8%98tefan_Ciobanu_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ștefan Ciobanu (politician)">Ștefan Ciobanu</a>, Romanian historian and academician, holds that the name was formed the same way as the name of <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99ineu-Cri%C8%99" title="Chișineu-Criș">Chișineu</a> (alternative spelling: Chișinău) in Western <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, near the border with Hungary. Its Hungarian name is <i>Kisjenő</i>, from which the Romanian name originates.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Kisjenő comes from <i>kis</i> "small" and the "Jenő," one of the seven <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian tribes">Hungarian tribes</a> that entered the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a> in 896. At least 24 other settlements are named after the "Jenő" tribe.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chișinău is known in Russian as Кишинёв (<i>Kishinyov</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Russian" title="Help:IPA for Russian">[kʲiʃɨˈnʲɔf]</a>]</span>). It is written <i>Kişinöv</i> in the Latin <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_alphabet" title="Gagauz alphabet">Gagauz alphabet</a>. It was also written as "Chișineu" in pre-20th-century Romanian<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and as "Кишинэу" in the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet">Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet</a>. Historically, the English language name for the city, "Kishinev", was based on the modified Russian one because it entered the English language via Russian at the time Chișinău was part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Kishinev_pogrom" title="Kishinev pogrom">Kishinev pogrom</a>). Therefore, it remains a common English name in some historical contexts. Otherwise, the Romanian-based "Chișinău" has been steadily gaining wider currency, especially in <a href="/wiki/Written_language" title="Written language">written language</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="History of Chișinău">History of Chișinău</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Timeline of Chișinău">Timeline of Chișinău</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moldavian_period">Moldavian period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Moldavian period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Founded in 1436 as a <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastery</a> village, the city was part of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Principality of Moldavia</a> (which, starting with the 16th century fell under the <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>). At the beginning of the 19th century Chișinău was a small town of 7,000 inhabitants.</p>
<p>In 1812, in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1806%E2%80%931812)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1806–1812)">Russo-Turkish War (1806–1812)</a>, the eastern half of Moldavia <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1812)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1812)">was ceded</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and Chișinău became the capital of the newly annexed <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblast</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia_Governorate" title="Bessarabia Governorate">Bessarabia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_period">Imperial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Imperial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg/220px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg/330px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg/440px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="715" data-file-height="496" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1889_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chișinău, 1889</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1834, an <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revival_architecture" title="Russian Revival architecture">imperial</a> townscape with broad and long roads had emerged as a result of a generous <a href="/wiki/Development_plan" title="Development plan">development plan</a>, which divided Chișinău roughly into two areas: the old part of the town — with its irregular building structures — and a newer city center and station. Between 26 May 1830 and 13 October 1836 the architect <a href="/wiki/Avraam_Melnikov" title="Avraam Melnikov">Avraam Melnikov</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_Cathedral,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Nativity Cathedral, Chișinău">Catedrala Nașterea Domnului</a> with a magnificent bell tower. In 1840 the building of the <a href="/wiki/Triumphal_arch,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Triumphal arch, Chișinău">Triumphal arch</a>, planned by the architect <a href="/w/index.php?title=Luca_Zaushkevich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Luca Zaushkevich (page does not exist)">Luca Zaushkevich</a>, was completed. Following this the construction of numerous buildings and landmarks began.</p>
<p>On 28 August 1871, Chișinău was linked by <a href="/wiki/Calea_Ferat%C4%83_din_Moldova" title="Calea Ferată din Moldova">rail</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, and in 1873 with <a href="/wiki/Corne%C8%99ti,_Moldova" title="Cornești, Moldova">Cornești</a>. Chișinău-<a href="/wiki/Ungheni" title="Ungheni">Ungheni</a>-<a href="/wiki/Ia%C8%99i" title="Iași">Iași</a> railway was opened on 1 June 1875 in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)</a>. The town played an important part in the war between Russia and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, as the main <a href="/wiki/Staging_area" title="Staging area">staging area</a> of the Russian invasion.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Belle_%C3%89poque" title="Belle Époque">Belle Époque</a>, the mayor of the city was <a href="/wiki/Carol_Schmidt" title="Carol Schmidt">Carol Schmidt</a>, considered one of Chisinau's best mayors. Its population had grown to 92,000 by 1862, and to 125,787 by 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pogroms_and_pre-revolution">Pogroms and pre-revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pogroms and pre-revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kishinev_pogrom" title="Kishinev pogrom">Kishinev pogrom</a></div>
<p>In the late 19th century, especially due to growing anti-Semitic sentiment in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and better economic conditions, many Jews chose to settle in Chișinău. By the year 1900, 43% of the population of Chișinău was Jewish — one of the highest numbers in Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A large <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">anti-Semitic</a> riot took place in the town on 6–7 April 1903, which would later be known as the <a href="/wiki/Kishinev_pogrom" title="Kishinev pogrom">Kishinev pogrom</a>. The rioting continued for three days, resulting in 47 Jews dead, 92 severely wounded, and 500 suffering minor injuries. In addition, several hundred houses and many businesses were plundered and destroyed. The pogroms are largely believed to have been incited by anti-Jewish propaganda in the only official newspaper of the time, <i>Bessarabetz</i> (<i>Бессарабецъ</i>). Mayor Schmidt disapproved of the incident and resigned later in 1903. The reactions to this incident included a petition to <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II of Russia</a> on behalf of <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">the American people</a> by the US President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> in July 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-pogrom_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pogrom-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 August 1905 another violent event occurred: The police opened fire on an estimated 3,000 demonstrating agricultural workers. Only a few months later, 19–20 October 1905, a further protest occurred, helping to force the hand of Nicholas II in bringing about the <a href="/wiki/October_Manifesto" title="October Manifesto">October Manifesto</a>. However, these demonstrations suddenly turned into another anti-Jewish pogrom, resulting in 19 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-pogrom_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pogrom-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanian_period">Romanian period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Romanian period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG/220px-SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG/330px-SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG/440px-SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SefanCelMare_Chisinau.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stephen the Great Monument</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the Russian <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, Bessarabia declared independence from the crumbling empire, as the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Democratic_Republic" title="Moldavian Democratic Republic">Moldavian Democratic Republic</a>, before joining the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Kingdom of Romania</a>. Romania granted important subsidies to its province and initiated large scale investment programs in the infrastructure of the main cities in Basarabia and Northern Bucovina, expanded the railroad infrastructure and started an extensive program to eradicate illiteracy. Only with the advent of modern technology and industrialization, it slowly rose into prominence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>As of 1919, Chișinău had an estimated population of 133,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaba_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaba-12">[12]</a></sup> Between 1918 and 1940 the center of the city undertook large <a href="/wiki/Renovation" title="Renovation">renovation</a> work. In 1927 the <a href="/wiki/Stephen_the_Great_Monument" title="Stephen the Great Monument">Stephen the Great Monument</a>, by the sculptor <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Pl%C4%83m%C4%83deal%C4%83" title="Alexandru Plămădeală">Alexandru Plămădeală</a>, was erected.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg/200px-Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg" width="200" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg/300px-Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg/400px-Moldova-chisineu-war-memorial-site.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="2015" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:State_Art_Museum_(80-ies)._(8257398062).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg/200px-State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg/300px-State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg/400px-State_Art_Museum_%2880-ies%29._%288257398062%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800" /></a>

<div class="thumb tright">

Dacia Boulevard in <a href="/wiki/Botanica_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanica District">Botanica District</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the chaos of the Second World War Chișinău was almost completely destroyed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.A devastating <a href="/wiki/1940_Vrancea_earthquake" title="1940 Vrancea earthquake">earthquake</a> occurred on 10 November 1940. The <a href="/wiki/Epicenter" title="Epicenter">epicenter</a> of the quake, which measured 7.3 on the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter scale</a>, was in eastern <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and subsequently led to substantial destruction.</p>
<p>After scarcely one year, the assault on the newly created <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian SSR</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> and Romanian armies began. Beginning with June 1941 the city came under bombardment by Nazi <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">air raids</a>. However, Romanian sources assign most of the responsibility for the damage to Soviet NKVD <a href="/wiki/Destruction_battalion" class="mw-redirect" title="Destruction battalion">destruction battalions</a>, that operated in Chișinău until 17 July 1941, when it was captured by invading Axis forces.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the German occupation, the city suffered from the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Nazi extermination policy</a> of its Jewish inhabitants, who were transported on trucks to the outskirts of the city and then summarily shot in partially dug pits. The number of Jews murdered during the initial occupation of the city is estimated at approximately 10,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the war drew to a conclusion, the city was once more pulled into heavy fighting as German and Romanian troops retreated. Chișinău was taken by the Red Army on 24 August 1944 as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_Offensive_(August_1944)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jassy–Kishinev Offensive (August 1944)">Jassy-Kishinev Operation</a>.</p>
<p>After the war, Bessarabia was fully integrated into the Soviet Union. Most of Bessarabia became the Moldavian SSR with Chișinău as its capital; around 30% of Bessarabia became parts of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian SSR</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_period">Soviet period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Soviet period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the years 1947 to 1949 the architect <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Shchusev" title="Alexey Shchusev">Alexey Shchusev</a> developed a plan with the aid of a team of architects for the gradual reconstruction of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>There was rapid population growth in the 1950s, to which the Soviet administration responded by constructing large-scale housing and palaces in the style of <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Stalinist architecture</a>. This process continued under <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a>, who called for construction under the slogan "good, cheaper and built faster". The new <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural style</a> brought about dramatic change and generated the style that dominates today, with large <a href="/wiki/Tower_block" title="Tower block">blocks of flats</a> arranged in considerable settlements.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The period of the most significant <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">redevelopment of the city</a> extended from 1971, when the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Soviet_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers (Soviet Union)">Council of Ministers</a> of the Soviet Union adopted a decision "On the measures for further development of the city of Kishinev", which secured more than one billion <a href="/wiki/Soviet_ruble" title="Soviet ruble">rubles</a> in investment from the <a href="/wiki/Budget" title="Budget">state budget</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> which continued until the independence of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> in 1991. On 4 March 1977 the city was again jolted by a terrible <a href="/wiki/1977_Vrancea_earthquake" title="1977 Vrancea earthquake">earthquake</a>. Several people were killed and panic broke out.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_independence">After independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: After independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(May 2012)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Many streets of Chișinău are <a href="/wiki/Street_names_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Street names in Chișinău">named after historic persons, places or events</a>. Independence from the Soviet Union was followed by a large-scale renaming of streets and localities from a Communist theme into a national one.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Chișinău is located on the river <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A2c_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Bâc River">Bâc</a>, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a>, at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;params=47_0_N_28_55_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">47°0′N</span> <span class="longitude">28°55′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">47.000°N 28.917°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">47.000; 28.917</span></span></span></a></span>, with an area of 120 square kilometres (46&#160;sq&#160;mi). The municipality comprises 635 square kilometres (245&#160;sq&#160;mi).</p>
<p>The city lies in central Moldova and is surrounded by a relatively level landscape with very fertile ground.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG/220px-RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG/330px-RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG/440px-RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RoseValley5_Chisinau.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose Valley</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chișinău has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa</i>) transitional with a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, characterized by hot dry summers and windy cold winters. Winter temperatures are often below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F), although they rarely drop below −10&#160;°C (14&#160;°F). In summer, the average maximum temperature is approximately 25&#160;°C (77&#160;°F), however, temperatures sometimes reach 35 to 40&#160;°C (95 to 104&#160;°F) in mid-summer in downtown. Although average <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a> during summer is low, there are infrequent yet heavy storms. Spring and autumn temperatures vary between 16 to 24&#160;°C (61 to 75&#160;°F), and precipitation during this time tends to be lower than in summer but with more frequent yet milder periods of rain.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG/220px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG/330px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG/440px-Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_4.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipality">Municipality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Municipality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Moldova is administratively subdivided into 3 municipalities, 32 districts, and 2 autonomous units. Chișinău is one of these municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides the city itself, the municipality comprises 34 other suburban localities: 6 towns (containing further 2 villages within), and 12 communes (containing further 14 villages within).</p>
<p>The estimated population, as of 2013, is shown in brackets:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg/200px-Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg.png" width="200" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg/300px-Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg/400px-Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="627" data-file-height="666" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_chisinau_vectorizata232.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Administrative sectors of Chișinău: 1-Centru, 2-Buiucani, 3-Rîșcani, 4-Botanica, 5-Ciocana</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chișinău is governed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_City_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chișinău City Council (page does not exist)">City Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Mayor of Chișinău">City Mayor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <span lang="ro" xml:lang="ro"><i>Primar</i></span>), both elected once every four years. The current mayor is <a href="/wiki/Dorin_Chirtoac%C4%83" title="Dorin Chirtoacă">Dorin Chirtoacă</a>.</p>
<p>His predecessor was <a href="/wiki/Serafim_Urechean" title="Serafim Urechean">Serafim Urechean</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova_(1994)" title="Constitution of Moldova (1994)">Moldovan constitution</a>, Urechean — elected to parliament in 2005 — was unable to hold an additional post to that of an <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Bloc_Democratic_Moldova" title="Electoral Bloc Democratic Moldova">Democratic Moldova Bloc</a> leader subsequently accepted his mandate and in April resigned from his former position. During his 11-year term, Urechean committed himself to the restoration of the church tower of the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_Cathedral,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Nativity Cathedral, Chișinău">Catedrala Nașterea Domnului</a> and improvements in public transport.</p>
<p>The current mayor, Dorin Chirtoacă from the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Moldova)" title="Liberal Party (Moldova)">Liberal party</a>, took office after elections in <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_local_elections,_2007" title="Moldovan local elections, 2007">June 2007</a>. Chirtoacă won reelections in <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_local_elections,_2011" title="Moldovan local elections, 2011">June 2011</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_local_elections,_2015" title="Moldovan local elections, 2015">June 2015</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The municipality in its totality elects a mayor and a local council, which then name five <i><a href="/wiki/Praetor#Recent_Praetors" title="Praetor">pretors</a></i>, one for each sector. They deal more locally with administrative matters. Each sector claims a part of the city and several suburbs:<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Historically, the city was home to fourteen factories in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaba_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaba-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chișinău is the financial and business capital of Moldova. Its GDP comprises about 60% of national economy<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> reached in 2012 the amount of 52 billion lei (US $4 billion). Thus, the GDP per capita of Chișinău stood at 227% of the Moldova's average. Chișinău has the largest and most developed mass media sector in Moldova, and is home to several related companies ranging from leading television networks and radio stations to major newspapers. All national and international banks (15) have their headquarters located in Chișinău.</p>
<p>Notable sites around Chișinău include the cinema Patria, the new malls <a href="/wiki/Malldova" title="Malldova">Malldova</a>, Megapolis Mall and best-known retailers, such as N1, Fidesco, Green Hills, Fourchette and Metro. While many locals continue to shop at the <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaars</a>, many upper class residents and tourists shop at the retail stores and at Malldova. Elăt, an older mall in the Botanica district, and Sun City, in the center, are more popular with locals.</p>
<p>Several amusement parks exist around the city. A <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> era one is in the Botanica district, along the three lakes of a major park, which reaches the outskirts of the city center. Another, the modern Aventura Park, is located farther from the center. A circus, which used to be in a grand building in the Rîșcani sector, has been inactive for several years due to a poorly funded renovation project.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">
<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th>
</tr>
<tr style="font-size:95%">

<p>According to the preliminary results of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Census_(2014)" title="Moldovan Census (2014)">last Moldovan census</a>, conducted between 12 and 25 May 2014, 492,894 inhabitants live within the Chișinău municipality limits, of whom 21,026 are currently working abroad. This represents a 16% drop in the number of residents as opposed to the results of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Census_(2004)" title="Moldovan Census (2004)">2004 Census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PopCensus2014_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopCensus2014-3">[3]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chișinău is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Orthodox_Church" title="Moldovan Orthodox Church">Moldovan Orthodox Church</a>, as well as of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Bessarabia" title="Metropolis of Bessarabia">Metropolis of Bessarabia</a>. The city has multiple churches and <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaba_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaba-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christians</a> – 90.0%
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christians">Orthodox Christians</a> – 88.4%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> – 1.2%
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> – 0.6%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> – 0.4%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> – 0.2%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> 0.1%</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a> – 0.4%</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Other – 1.0%</li>
<li>No religion – 1.4%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atheists" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheists">Atheists</a> – 1.5%</li>
<li>Undeclared – 6.1%</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1208px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg" class="image" title="Panorama of Chișinău"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg/1200px-Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg" width="1200" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg/1800px-Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg/2400px-Telegentru_at_night_panorama_01.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="10486" data-file-height="1368" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Panorama of Chișinău</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_MNAIM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Museum_MNAIM.jpg/220px-Museum_MNAIM.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Museum_MNAIM.jpg/330px-Museum_MNAIM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Museum_MNAIM.jpg/440px-Museum_MNAIM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="544" data-file-height="363" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_MNAIM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_History_of_Moldova" title="National Museum of History of Moldova">National Museum of History of Moldova</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chișinău's growth plan was developed in the 19th century. In 1836 the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Kishinev_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Kishinev Cathedral">Kishinev Cathedral</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Bell_tower" title="Bell tower">belfry</a> was finished. The belfry was demolished in Soviet times and was rebuilt in 1997. Chișinău also displays a tremendous number of orthodox churches and 19th century buildings around the city such as <a href="/wiki/Ciuflea_Monastery" title="Ciuflea Monastery">Ciuflea Monastery</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_Church,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Transfiguration Church, Chișinău">Transfiguration Church</a>.</p>
<p>Much of the city is made from limestone dug from <a href="/wiki/Cricova" title="Cricova">Cricova</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, leaving a famous <a href="/wiki/Cricova_(winery)" title="Cricova (winery)">wine cellar</a> there.</p>
<p>Many modern-style buildings have been built in the city since 1991. There are many office and shopping complexes that are modern, renovated or newly built, including Kentford, SkyTower, and <a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%B3n_Fenosa" title="Unión Fenosa">Union Fenosa</a> headquarters. However, the old Soviet-style clusters of living blocks are still an extensive feature of the cityscape.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_education">Culture and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_schools_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="List of public schools in Chișinău">List of public schools in Chișinău</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Moldova" title="List of universities in Moldova">List of universities in Moldova</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg/220px-Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg/330px-Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg/440px-Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="498" data-file-height="331" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_Opera_Teatr060709_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moldova_National_Opera_Ballet" title="Moldova National Opera Ballet">National Opera and Ballet Theatre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is home to 12 public and 11 private universities, the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_Moldova" title="Academy of Sciences of Moldova">Academy of Sciences of Moldova</a>, a number of institutions offering high school and 1–2 years of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">college education</a>.</p>
<p>In Chișinău there are several museums. The three national museums are The National Museum of Ethnography &amp; Natural History, the National Museum of Arts and the National Museum of Archaeology &amp; History.</p>
<p>American sculptor <a href="/wiki/Moissaye_Marans" title="Moissaye Marans">Moissaye Marans</a> was born in Chișinău in 1902.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_and_festivals">Events and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Events and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chișinău, as well as Moldova as a whole, still show signs of ethnic culture. Signs that say "Patria Mea" (English: My homeland) can be found all over the capital. While few people still wear traditional Moldavian attire, large public events often draw in such original costumes.</p>
<p><i>Moldova National Wine Day</i> and <i>Wine Festival</i> take place every year in the first weekend of October, in Chișinău. The events celebrate the fall harvest and recognizes the country's long history of winemaking, which dates back some 500 years.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first radio station in Chișinău, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Basarabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Basarabia">Radio Basarabia</a>, was launched by the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Radio_Broadcasting_Company" title="Romanian Radio Broadcasting Company">Romanian Radio Broadcasting Company</a> on 8 October 1939, when the religious service was broadcast on air from the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_Cathedral,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Nativity Cathedral, Chișinău">Nativity Cathedral</a>. The first TV station in the city, <a href="/wiki/Moldova_1" title="Moldova 1">Moldova 1</a>, was launched on 30 April 1958, while <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Lupan" title="Nicolae Lupan">Nicolae Lupan</a> was serving as the redactor-in-chief of <a href="/wiki/TeleRadio-Moldova" title="TeleRadio-Moldova">TeleRadio-Moldova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of Moldova's <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media industry</a> is based in Chișinău. The state national broadcaster in the country is the <a href="/wiki/Public_ownership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public ownership">state-owned</a> <a href="/wiki/Moldova_1" title="Moldova 1">Moldova 1</a>, which has its head office in the city. The broadcasts of <a href="/wiki/TeleRadio-Moldova" title="TeleRadio-Moldova">TeleradioMoldova</a> have been criticized by the Independent Journalism Center as showing 'bias' towards the authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> There are some hopes that a new broadcasting code will resolve some of these issues.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pro_TV" title="Pro TV">Pro TV</a> Chișinău broadcasts locally. It was repeatedly denied national license by the communist government and threatened to be closed down. The station broadcasts a mixture of independent <a href="/wiki/Local_news" title="Local news">local news</a>, in addition to entertainment and documentary programs from Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other TV channels are <a href="/wiki/PRIME" class="mw-redirect" title="PRIME">PRIME</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurnal_TV" title="Jurnal TV">Jurnal TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Publika_TV" title="Publika TV">Publika TV</a>, CTC, <a href="/wiki/DTV_(Moldovan_TV_channel)" title="DTV (Moldovan TV channel)">DTV</a>, Euro TV, MTV, MuzTV, NIT and TV 7. In addition to television, most Moldovan radio and newspaper companies have their headquarters in the city. Broadcasters include the national radio Vocea Basarabiei, Prime FM, BBC Moldova, Europa Libera, Kiss FM, Pro FM, Radio 21, Fresh FM (Romanian <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio station</a> Național FM), Radio Nova, Russkoe radio, Hit FM, and many others.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Unimedia.md" title="Unimedia.md">Unimedia.md</a> is the most visited portal.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Others portals are Jurnal.md, News.yam.md, and Union.md.</p>
<p>The biggest broadcasters are SunTV, Satellit and Zebra TV. In 2007 SunTV and Zebra launched <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital TV</a> cable networks.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_International_Airport" title="Chișinău International Airport">Chișinău International Airport</a> offers connections to major destinations, within Europe and Asia.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Air_Moldova" title="Air Moldova">Air Moldova</a> flight operator has its head office on the grounds of Chișinău International Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most popular form of internal <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Moldova" title="Transport in Moldova">transport in Moldova</a> is generally the <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although the city has just three main terminals, buses generally serve as the <a href="/wiki/Mode_of_transport" title="Mode of transport">means of transport</a> between cities in and outside of Moldova. Popular destinations include <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> (Ukraine), <a href="/wiki/Ia%C8%99i" title="Iași">Iași</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> (Romania).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The second most popular form of domestic transportation within Moldova is via railways. The total length of the network managed by <a href="/wiki/Calea_Ferat%C4%83_din_Moldova" title="Calea Ferată din Moldova">Moldovan Railway CFM</a> (as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) is 1,232 kilometers (766 miles). The entire network is single track and is not electrified. The central hub of all railways is <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_Railway_Station" title="Chișinău Railway Station">Chișinău Central Railway Station</a>. There is another smaller railway station - Revaca located on the city's ends.</p>
<p>Chișinău Railway Station has an international railway terminal with connections to <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Samara,_Russia" title="Samara, Russia">Samara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">Varna</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>. Due to the simmering conflict between Moldova and the unrecognised <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria republic</a> the rail traffic towards Ukraine is occasionally stopped.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trolleybuses">Trolleybuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Trolleybuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Trolleybuses in Chișinău">Trolleybuses in Chișinău</a></div>
<p>There is wide <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> network operating as common public transportation within city. From 1994, Chișinău saw the establishment of new trolleybus lines, as well as an increase in capacity of existing lines, to improve connections between the urban districts. The network comprises 22 trolleybus lines being 246&#160;km (153&#160;mi) in length. Trolleybuses run between 06:00 and 23:00. There are 270 units daily operating in Chișinău. However the requirements are as minimum as 340 units. Trolleybus ticket costs at about 2 lei (ca. <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">$</a>0.18). It is the cheapest method of transport within Chișinău municipality.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are 29 lines of buses within Chișinău municipality. At each public transportation stops there is attached a schedule for buses and trolleybuses. There are approximately 330 public transportation stops within Chișinău municipality. There is a big lack of buses inside city limits, with only 105 buses operating within Chișinău.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minibuses">Minibuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Minibuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Chișinău and its suburbs, privately operated minibuses, known as "<a href="/wiki/Rutiera" class="mw-redirect" title="Rutiera">rutieras</a>" generally follow the major bus and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> routes and appear more frequently.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There are approx. 1800 units of minibuses operating within Chișinău. Minibuses services are priced the same as buses - 3 <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_leu" title="Moldovan leu">lei</a> for a ticket (ca. $0.25).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traffic">Traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city traffic becomes more and more congested each year pass. Nowadays there are at about 300,000 cars in the city plus 100,000 transit transport coming everyday to the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Prospective number of personal transport will reach the 550,000 (without transit) in 2025.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/220px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/330px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/440px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="765" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/FC_Zimbru_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="FC Zimbru Chișinău">FC Zimbru</a> Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are three professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> clubs in Chișinău, all playing in the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_National_Division" title="Moldovan National Division">Divizia Națională</a> (national league): <a href="/wiki/FC_Zimbru_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="FC Zimbru Chișinău">Zimbru</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Dacia_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="FC Dacia Chișinău">Dacia</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Academia_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="FC Academia Chișinău">Academia</a>. Of the larger public multiuse stadiums in the city is the Stadionul Dinamo (Dinamo Stadium), which has a capacity of 2,692. The <a href="/wiki/Zimbru_Stadium" title="Zimbru Stadium">Zimbru Stadium</a>, opened in May 2006 with a capacity of 10,500 sitting places, meets all the requirements for holding official international matches, and was the venue for all <a href="/wiki/Moldova_national_football_team" title="Moldova national football team">Moldova</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> qualifying games. Currently there are discussions to build a new modern olympic stadium with capacity of circa 25,000 seats, that would meet all international requirements.</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Rayel" title="Andrew Rayel">Andrew Rayel</a>, Stage name of Andrei Rata, Moldovan DJ;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ulanovsky" title="Alexander Ulanovsky">Alexander Ulanovsky</a>, the chief illegal "<a href="/wiki/Rezident" class="mw-redirect" title="Rezident">rezident</a>" for Soviet Military Intelligence (GRU), prisoner in the Soviet gulag;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Zemurray" title="Sam Zemurray">Sam Zemurray</a>, American businessman who made his fortune in the banana trade;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maria_Cebotari" title="Maria Cebotari">Maria Cebotari</a>, Romanian soprano and actress, one of Europe's greatest opera stars in the 1930s and 1940s</li>
</ul>
